1068	2	2017-07-06 16:23:05.113	2011-06-13 07:35:32.507	mjkruse	johnemm	Business Letters Describing the Financial Market in Cuba		1867	1871	NULL	NULL	NULL	118 handwritten letters (over 200 total pages)			Special and Area Studies Collections, George A. Smathers Libraries, University of Florida	Apfelbaum, Charles	0	2004	4	x		2004-09-01 00:00:00.000	Manuscripts - Latin American and Caribbean Collections	Collection of handwritten letters dated 1867-1871 and written by various agents in Cuba reporting on business conditions to merchants in Portland, Maine. Most of the letters are addressed to J.B. Brown and Sons or to Churchill, Browns and Manson. The letters report the market prices and sales of molasses, sugar, shooks (knock-down barrels), and other commodities. Additionally, they discuss market conditions, agricultural concerns, grinding and manufacturing activities, and shipping. Descriptions of the ships and which cargoes are selling or not selling are also provided. |  | The letters are written from such places as Havana, Mataurus, Caibarien, Cardenas, and Sagua La Grande. The agents include Vanderkreft, La Puerta and Co.; D. Ruiz Toledo; Smith and Company; Juan Ferrin; L.Y. Stocker and Co.; J.C. Burnham and Co.; and C.P. Madan. The majority of the letters are written in English, but a small number are written in Spanish. King, a University of Florida graduate student, wrote a dissertation on the Seminoles and worked for the Southeastern Indian Oral History Project. 1638	6	2017-08-17 16:39:20.980	2012-04-24 13:34:34.207	mjkruse	mvargasb	Lillian Guerra Collection	1890-1900, 1920-1953, 2013	NULL	NULL	NULL	NULL	1.24	3 boxes	Linear feet	Guerra, Lillian	Special and Area Studies Collections, George A. Smathers Libraries, University of Florida		0	2012	5	0207		2012-02-07 00:00:00.000	Manuscripts - Latin American and Caribbean Collections	The Lillian Guerra Collection includes photographs, historical documents and ephemeral objects related to Cuba’s struggle for independence, social life, Cuban enterprises, and political parties. |  | This collection includes a collection of portraits from the early 20th century taken at various photographic studios in Havana, photographs from the late 19th century showing Cubans involved in the struggle for independence, correspondence between Tomás Estrada Palma and Juan Francisco O’Farrill, a commemorative sculpture and coin of José Martí, and documents and ephemeral material related to the Partido del Pueblo Cubano and Partido Comunista de Cuba. |  | *NOTE - The following is sensitive information not to be added to the public finding aid until determined to no longer be a sensitive issue.* |  | Notes on the Lillian Guerra Collection |  | Lillian Guerra obtained the collection of Cuban badges from the family of Orlando Milián, Sr. Milián was a member of the Communist Party. He was Fidel Castro Diaz-Balart’s (the son of Comandante Fidel Castro) bodyguard. Each of the medals in the collection depicts significant events and commemorates the owner’s achievements in Cuban politics, academics, and cultural programs. In 1993, when Cuba underwent a great transformation due to the fall of the USSR, Milián, like many Cubans, felt abandoned and betrayed.  Castro’s government denied that a change was taking place, and that even though slowly, they were heading towards capitalism. Milián quit the Communist Party circa 2005.  At that point, the medals lost significance for him. |  | Guerra obtained the documents related to Juan Francisco O'Farrill from the O'Farrill family while she was doing research for her dissertation on José Martí. She made a reference to this documents on Chapter 2 of her book The Myth of José Martí: Conflicting Nationalisms in Early Twentieth-century Cuba. | 			Gift	NULL	NULL	NULL		2017-06-12 00:00:00.000			0	0	Waiting on cataloging			Donated by Lillian Guerra in four separate accessions in 2012, 2013, 2015, and 2017. 1644	3	2012-06-27 19:53:24.967	2012-06-18 09:15:36.140	johnemm	carvann	Leon Pomerance Papers		NULL	NULL	NULL	NULL	NULL			Pomerance, Leon	Special and Area Studies Collections, George A. Smathers Libraries, University of Florida	Hartigan, Karelisa	0	2011	17	x		2011-01-01 00:00:00.000	Manuscripts - General Collections				Gift	NULL	NULL	NULL		NULL			0	0				The Leon Pomerance Collection arrived at the University of Florida Special Collections Archives by way of Blake Landor. Landor worked beside Karelisa Hartigan who taught in the Classics Department for many years. Hartigan collected the materials for her work on Leon Pomerance’s biography. Ultimately, her work culminated in an article included in the Biographical Information section, “Leon Pomerance: An Archaeological Philanthropist.” The items were acquired mainly by her correspondence with Marc Rosenblum, Leon Pomerance’s brother-in-law, husband to his late wife’s older sister Nettie. Hartigan also gained the materials by way of Pomerance’s sons Bernard and Michael, and also through the various museums that had held Pomerance’s art collections, or had pieces donated by Pomerance. Some items also arrived through Hartigan’s inquiries to such organizations as the AIA, which Pomerance led, and also institutions where Pomerance had lectured or where his contemporaries still worked.  |  |  | 				NULL	NULL	NULL	NULL	NULL	NULL	NULL	NULL	NULL		NULL	NULL	NULL	NULL	NULL	NULL	NULL	NULL	ufms314.xml							1

Smathers Libraries, University of Florida	Szok, Peter, Dr., Professor, Department of History	0	2014	12	0428		2014-04-28 00:00:00.000	Manuscripts - Latin American and Caribbean Collections	The Peter Szok Images document Panama’s long and important tradition of popular art.  Popular art bloomed in the mid-twentieth century when thousands of U.S. soldiers arrived to protect the canal from a potential Axis attack and fostered a lively Cuban music scene.  Popular art draws on Afro-Caribbean aesthetics and appears in cantinas, buses, and in similar working-class venues.  The collection contains images of numerous paintings as well as photos of the leading artists, many of whom are of Afro-Panamanian descent.  Featured painters include Andrés Salazar, José Ángel Ruiloba, Jorge Dunn, Ramón Enrique Hormi, Teodoro de Jesús Villarué, Justino Fernández, Óscar Melgar, Luis Evans, and Oliver Bruce. Smathers Libraries, University of Florida		0	2014	10	0401		2014-04-01 00:00:00.000	Manuscripts - Judaica Collections	Personal archive of Private Richard Michael Feist (Service No. 14458550, East Surrey Regiment). Feist was a member of the Jewish Brigade and was transferred to the Search Division of the British Army of the Rhine (BAOR) which was responsible for tracing missing persons.	The archive contains | • unique manuscript material – large quantities of letters in several languages relating to the search for missing relatives | • internal secret British army documents relating to Jewish DPs | • rare cyclostyled newsletters | • list of missing persons in the months and early years after camp liberation | • cyclostyled history of the Search Bureau | • report on the Search in Belsen | • 3 page typed diary in German of the last days of Buchenwald before liberation | • handwritten list of camps and the current situation in them  | • report on on Sandbostel Camp | • list of information on Breslau Jews |  | The archive contains several different categories of documents: | • A collection of personal documents relating to Richard Feist including his army rations, callup papers, letters from the Army to his home address etc. | • Over 100 letters in English which included requests for assistance | • Approx. 80 German letters to Feist requesting help searching for family members | • Approximately 50 letters in Hebrew to Feist | • A photographic album showing members of the search committee | • Letters from various organizations such as the World Jewish Congress etc | • Official forms requesting information pertaining to missing persons | • Samples of certificates given to people who helped. |  | This important archive is an extensive body of primary source material that will assist researchers to understand the process and logistics needed to address the huge task of searching for missing persons created in the aftermath of the Holocaust. It will help to: | • establish the names of those who perished in the Holocaust and where possible, their place and date of death. | • analyse the departments and organizations involved including the Search Bureau for Missing Persons run by the BAOR, UNWRA and the Jewish Agency | • demonstrate how documentation was used for obtaining information - the archive includes relevant forms such as the Search Bureau Control Commission–Enquiry Concerning Missing Persons Forms ( BAOR) , and DP registration form issued by the American Expeditionary Force (AEP) | • understand the personal anguish and distress felt by relatives searching for missing persons through the letters Feist received.  | 		Purchase	NULL	NULL	NULL		2015-04-01 00:00:00.000			1	0	Aleph: 033669283 | OCLC: 921436859 | 			Purchased from: |  Fishburn Books | 43 Ridge Hill | Golders Green | London NW11 8PR | Tel 0208 455 9139, Fax 0208 922 5008 | fishburnbooks@yahoo.co.uk | www.fishburnbooks.com | http://www.fishburnbooks.com/catalogs/January2012JudaicaListJan16thLatest.pdf			Processed	NULL	NULL	NULL	1	NULL	NULL	2015-09-18 00:00:00.000	NULL	NULL		NULL	NULL	NULL	NULL	NULL	NULL	NULL	NULL								1

1775	2	2017-09-07 10:43:23.707	2016-07-11 09:43:40.693	mjkruse	steveduckworth	La Colectividad Israelita al Ex Director de Inmigración D. Juan A. Alsina	1910	NULL	NULL	NULL	NULL	1	Large 4to. (330 x 270mm). Presentation album.	Volume		Special and Area Studies Collections, George A. Smathers Libraries, University of Florida		0	2016	0002			2016-05-23 00:00:00.000	Manuscripts - Judaica Collections	Title: La Colectividad Israelita al Ex Director de Inmigración D. Juan A. Alsina. | Author: ARGENTINA (Jewish Immigration) | Publisher: San Fernando (Argentina), 1910. | Book ID: 5624 | Price: GBP 6500.0 | Description: Large 4to. (330 x 270mm). Presentation album comprising 40 thick cardboard leaves with 1052 legible autograph signatures in ink on 74 pages, many in Cyrillic script. Title-page with fine allegorical full-page watercolour painting signed by F. Fortuny, on verso a full-page calligraphic presentation inscription. Brocade-patterned endpapers. Bound in contemporary maroon cowhide with gilt borders; front cover decorated with an elaborate chased brass floral ornament (220 x 155mm) incorporating a shield engraved with the inscription 'La Colectividad Israelita al Doctor Juan A. Alsina', flanked by the seated figure of Hermes with herald's staff and anchor, and by the allegorical figure of 'Argentina', as an earth goddess, standing to the right, holding a sheaf of grain, a sickle, fruits and flowers. Original brass clasps and catches intact; rich inner gilt dentelles; edges gilt. A superbly produced de luxe album presented by the Argentine Jewish community to the retiring Director of the Immigration Authority, Dr Juan Antonio Alsina (1852-1937), a highly respected civil servant and decorated academician, founder of the Historical Museum of La Plata, author and publisher. The album containing over a thousand autograph signatures of Russian Jewish immigrants especially collected for the occasion represents a symbolic gesture of appreciation and gratitude by the Argentine Jewish community at that time largely originating from Russia. The prefatory address refers to the welcoming and sympathetic help extended by the dedicatee who had carried out his duties with distinction for twenty years. Alsina had the difficult task of regulating the massive immigration of this period and having to negotiate with foreign governments to that end. He is the author of a 2-volume work on the Argentine worker, and two authoritative books on European immigration to Argentina. The allegorical title painting signed ' F. Fortuny' shows the seated figure of Argentina with a Phrygian cap upholding the national arms with her right hand, with her left beckoning toward two immigrants: an old man with a beard (perhaps a Moses figure) supporting himself by leaning on a youth and a walking stick, with the words 'beneficios y libertad para todos los hombres del mundo que quieren habitar en el suelo argentino' (rewards and freedom for all men of this world who want to live on Argentine soil); in the foreground the emblems of agriculture, industry and learning; in the background, grain fields, and beyond, a large steamer entering a harbour. Francisco Fortuny (1865-1942) was a distinguished artist who painted scenes of cultural and historical significance in Argentine history. His famous painting ' The Congress of Tucumán, the Declaration of Independence of Argentina from Spain in 1816' is celebrated. Apart from insignificant traces of light foxing because of the quality of the paper, the album is in remarkably good condition. It is offered together with a separately printed festschrift (dated 18 December 1910) of 48 pages of text in Spanish, Hebrew, and Russian, containing the laudatory addresses of the presentation commission, and Alsina's reply. The members of the commission were M. Sigal, David Elkin, Dr Henry Joseph, Dr Alejandro Zabotinsky, Naum Enquin, Jacobo Joseievich & Arnoldo Elkin. Eight of the nine illustrations are photographic plates: these include a portrait of the dedicatee serving as a frontispiece, portrayals of the presentation commission and festivities, and reproductions of the front cover of the presentation album, its frontispiece, and a medal. Original wrappers (lower blank margin repaired, a stain in blank tailend margin of second leaf). Title within art nouveau border using Hebrew symbols. Smathers Libraries, University of Florida		0	2016	0005			2016-12-15 00:00:00.000		This bulletin was published after the Cuban Revolution, which officially ended on January 1, 1959. The publication highlights the nation's growth since then and documents important historical moments, including the resignation of President Manuel Urrutia Lleó as shown on its cover. The narration of this section declares how Urrutia was an adequate candidate at the time of his instatement into the presidency, but has over time lost sight of the public's needs and the post-revolutionary goals of the nation. Additionally, it briefly touches on the controversy between Urrutia and Fidel Castro. The following pages of the bulletin state the dissatisfaction of the Cuban government with the foreign opinion of Cuba. The effects of the revolution on the public and a meeting of the Americas' countries to take place in Santiago, Chile among the countries of the Americas are also discussed. The publication also mentions aspects of arts and culture, such as innovations in Cuban theater and cinema. It also includes images of paintings of working artists of that time, including works by Servando Cabrera and Amelia González. The last few pages of the bulletin provide excerpts on Cuba's economy, in the realms of the sugar and mining industries, the current state of the Zapata Swamp, and a section with bits of information titled as “Miscellaneous”. Smathers Libraries, University of Florida		0	2017	0006			2016-01-01 00:00:00.000	Manuscripts - Latin American and Caribbean Collections	Circular distributed by Envoy Francisco Tacon, brother to Cuba's controversial Governor, Miguel Tacon. The document urges vigilance of the comings and goings of American vessels in Cuba, discussing in particular the shipment of weapons, arms, and uniforms for the army headed to any port in Europe or America. He instructs them to keep a particular eye on the shipment of the vessel "Coyo." His circular closes by warning that any who withold information will be held responsible by the Spanish government, under order of the Queen. |  | This vigilance of the exportation of American goods in Cuba may be a result of an order passed by the United States in June of 1834 which addressed tariffs placed on Spanish vessels trading in America. Though the new fees were not to be enforced until the following March, it appears that Tacon is preemptively surveying the shipments of American vessels, possibly to negotiate better terms for Spain.		Circular is separated at center fold, small loss affecting one word of text. Smathers Libraries, University of Florida		0	2017	0014			2017-03-13 00:00:00.000	University Archives - Photograph Collection	Harold Campbell Stansfield, Class of 1924, was listed as a student at the University of Florida from 1919 to 1924. He received his commission as a second lieutenant on May 29, 1923 and his bachelor’s in mechanical engineering in May, 1924. The student register lists his hometown as Bradenton.  A military draft record for 1917-1918 indicates he was born December 5, 1899.  |  | Consists of loose pages and fragments from a photograph album owned by student Harold Campbell Stansfield. The photographs appear to be from the late 1910s and early 1920s. Among the places that can be identified outside of Gainesville are Atlanta, Stone Mountain, Tampa and Miami. Many of the photographs were taken at Camp McClellan, later Fort McClellan, a military post outside Anniston, Alabama. It’s possible that Stansfield was being trained at Camp McClellan when World War I ended, but it is more likely that he was sent there as part of ROTC training at the University of Florida. Among the scenes depicted at UF are Warren’s Cave, dorm rooms, and flag rush. There are many photographs of trains, ships and cars. Of special note are images of players and managers from the Boston Braves and at least one of a New York Giants player. These may have been taken in 1919 when the Giants used Fleming Field as a spring training facility.  |  | The album is similar in content to that of Jackson Henson McDonald, who was a classmate of Stansfield.  | 			Gift	NULL	NULL	NULL		2017-03-13 00:00:00.000			1	0	Aleph: 978348223 | OCLC: 035037015			Provenance is unclear. Eugene Grissom’s ephemeral resource material, used for his research activities as a founding member of the Frank Rosolino Memorial Scholarship for Jazz Trombone (International Trombone Association), co -founder of The Frank Rosolino Memorial Fund and for his many Frank Rosolino biographical publications (FOND MEMORIES OF FRANK ROSOLINO, etc.), is contained in Box 7. Professor Grissom used a hard copy of the epic 60 YEARS OF RECORDED JAZZ (created by Belgian musicologist Walter Bruyninckx) in support of his historical trombone research. The 8000 plus pages were stored in numbered cardboard sleeves by Professor Grissom. The pages have been removed from these acidic sleeves and foldered, according to Grissom’s numbering system, in boxes 8 through 13. The researcher will notice some alphabetized sections are out of sequence. According to Professor Grissom this is due to updates, corrections and supplements that were added as they arrived by mail. Board of Control Case. No. 21.138. In 1949, at the age of 41, Virgil D. Hawkins applied for admission to the all-white law school at the University of Florida in Gainesville and was rejected because he was black. Mr. Hawkins challenged the state's segregated school system. In 1956, the United States Supreme Court ruled that he should be admitted to the school. |  | But the Florida Supreme Court invoked the doctrine of states' rights to deny him admission. The state's Board of Control then adopted rigid entrance requirements that made it impossible for Mr. Hawkins to enroll. |  | In 1976 the Florida Bar urged the Florida Supreme Court to allow Mr. Hawkins to take the state bar examination even though he had attended an unaccredited law school in Massachusetts 20 years earlier. The bar said he should be given special consideration because of his ill treatment while he was trying to enter law school in 1949. |  | In November 1976, the Florida Supreme Court ruled 7-0 that Mr. Hawkins should be allowed to practice law and waived a requirement that he first take the bar exam. Smathers Libraries, University of Florida		0	2017	0026			1962-01-01 00:00:00.000	Manuscripts - Popular Culture Collections	The Belknap Theatre Broadside Collection forms part of the Belknap Collection for the Performing Arts. Originally founded as a dance archive, in 1953, the Belknap Collection has expanded through purchases and donations to include other areas of popular culture, including theatre, cinema, and music. This particular collection of broadsides was acquired during the tenure of Sara Yancey Belknap, purchased from the John and Mable Ringling Museum of Art in 1962. |  | The collection contains 1,184 broadsides advertising theatrical performances in the United States and Great Britain. The broadsides are single sheets, and typically one sided. The bulk of the broadsides are from the 19th century, with very few from the early 20th century. They have been arranged roughly by size (small, medium, large and extra-large) and then filed alphabetically, by the title of the most prominent production on each broadside, within 10 folders. The final folder in the collection includes extra-large items, as well as broadsides that were found later in the organizational process that could not be easily integrated with those already organized and labeled.  |  | Each individual broadside has a description. The description generally contains the title of the major production advertised, the measurements of the broadside, and the year of the performance, if noted. The name of the venue where the performance takes place and geographical information is included when it is evident. In many cases the broadsides were advertising whole programs that included multiple productions; the titles of these additional plays are often included in the description. Also included in the description are any performers who have been clearly marked as headlining in the respective performances.      | 			Purchase	NULL	NULL	NULL		2017-04-27 00:00:00.000			1	0	Aleph: 035135413 | OCLC: 988941973			Purchased from the John and Mable Ringling Museum of Art in Sarasota. 1818	2	2017-10-30 11:58:37.303	2017-05-31 11:37:53.477	mjkruse	mjkruse	Steven F. Lawson Research Papers		1949	1985	1949	1963	1.74	3 boxes	Linear feet	Lawson, Steven F.	Special and Area Studies Collections, George A. Smathers Libraries, University of Florida		0	2017.0030				2016-01-01 00:00:00.000	Manuscripts - Florida History Collections	The Steven F. Lawson Collection research papers contain copies of materials collected by Lawson and used for the publication of two articles.  The first box contains files on the Groveland, Fla., case, in which four African-American men, Charles Greenlee, Samuel Shepherd, Walter Irvin, and Earnest Thomas, were charged in the rape of a white woman.  Content includes copies of newspaper clippings, articles, interviews, and documents from archives such as the Archives of Labor History and Urban Affairs at Wayne State University, the Library of Congress, and the Florida State Archives in Tallahassee.  There are separate files of materials on Walter Irvin, Willis McCall, (the sheriff who shot Irvin and Shepherd while transporting them from Raiford State Prison to Lake County ), and Harry T.  Moore. (Moore, who was the executive secretary of the NAACP in Florida, had been raising money to support the Groveland defendants and sought to have McCall removed from office.)  The material also includes handwritten notes and Lawson’s research correspondence. The case was the subject of Steven F. Lawson, David R. Colburn, and Darryl Paulson’s article, “Groveland: Florida’s Little Scottsboro,” which appeared in the Florida Historical Quarterly in 1986.    |  | Boxes two and three include materials related to the Florida Legislative Investigation Committee, also known as the Johns Committee.  Members of the committee sought to connect members of the National Association for the Advancement of Colored People (NAACP) to communism in order to undermine its efforts at desegregation.  Most of the information Lawson collected was about the Revered Theodore R. Gibson.  Gibson, an Episcopalian priest, served as the president of the Miami branch of the NAACP.  When called before the Johns Committee, he agreed to answer questions about specific individuals who were suspected to be communists, but he refused to provide the membership list for the organization.  Gibson faced a contempt charge, which included a $1200 dollar fine and jail time, but the Supreme Court of the United States overturned his conviction. Files consist of copies of journal articles, hearing transcripts, and drafts of the Supreme Court decision and also include material on race relations and segregation in Florida and other individuals investigated by the Johns Committee, including Sheriff Hugh Lewis and NAACP lawyers accused of ethics violations and investigated by the Florida Bar.  Lawson used these materials to write “The Florida Legislative Investigation Committee and the Constitutional Readjustment of Race Relations, 1956-1963,” which appeared in An Uncertain Tradition: Constitutionalism and the History of the South (University of Georgia Press, 1989). | 			Gift	NULL	NULL	NULL		2017-05-31 00:00:00.000			1	0	Aleph: 035135474 | OCLC: 988943368 |  | 			Steven F. Lawson donated the collection to the Department of Special and Area Studies Collections in 2016. Smathers Libraries, University of Florida		0	2017	0031			2016-12-11 00:00:00.000	Manuscripts - Judaica Collections	Aileen Josephs, née Walborsky, was born in Mexico City in 1964. This collection is dedicated to her father Hyman Walborsky’s memory. His family immigrated to the Unites States from Poland. Hyman’s father, Israel Wolborsky left Poland for the US in 1923, after his marriage to Sara Miadovitch. She and their firstborn son Hershel, later Harry (1924-2002), followed Israel in 1929 to America. Hyman, the younger son (and Aileen’s father) was born in New York in 1931. It is unclear if Hyman or his elder brother Harry changed the family name to Walborsky. After serving in Korea, Hyman worked for the underwear company Exquisite Form. The company sent him to various Latin American countries as representative and to set up factories. He met his future wife and Aileen’s mother Aura Navarro in Maracay, Venezuela. Harry became a chemistry professor and taught until his retirement in Florida State University, Tallahassee, Florida. |  | Aileen was born in Mexico to where Exquisite Form sent his father to set up a factory. She spent her childhood in Mexico. In 1982 she enrolled in Brandeis University and continued her studies at Boston College Law School. She became an immigration activist and studied immigration law. For her senior thesis, she conducted fieldwork among the Salvadorian community in Waltham, Massachusetts and advocated the establishment of a statutory type of safe haven for refugees from warzones and regions afflicted by natural disaster. She completed her studies cum laude and her human rights advocacy became her calling as an immigration lawyer. With her husband she decided to move to Florida and in addition to her legal practice, she works as Guatemala’s honorary consul. Their son is a graduate of the University of Florida. | 		Two prayer books and a document were sent to conservation. These items were never returned to special collections and are presumed to be lost somewhere at the off-site ILF facility where conservation services are located. 1824	6	2017-10-30 12:03:31.020	2017-06-05 09:10:00.887	mjkruse	mjkruse	Cuban Slave Death Certificates and Burial Letters Collection		1850	1891	NULL	NULL	1		Folder		Special and Area Studies Collections, George A. Smathers Libraries, University of Florida	William Reese Company.	0	2017	0036			2016-12-21 00:00:00.000	Manuscripts - Latin American and Caribbean Collections	28 eight Manuscript Documents and Printed Forms Reporting the Deaths and Illnesses of Current and Former Slaves in 19th-Century Cuba. |  | Cuba, 1891. [28] leaves, various sizes. Eighteen manuscript leaves and ten printed forms completed in manuscript. Some browning and chipping, with occasional worming and paper loss, sometimes affecting text. Several documents with contemporary Cuban institutional ink stamps. Good plus. A collection of twenty-eight death reports and other notices for Cuban slaves and freedmen from the second half of the 19th century. The vast majority of the notices report a death or burial, giving a brief description of the slave or other Cuban person of color, usually including skin tone, country or region of origin, owners or relations if known, cause of death (which include illnesses such as typhoid and epilepsy), and give the date. Most documents are accomplished entirely in manuscript, however there is a significant portion of the group that consist of completed printed forms, both written in quite legible hands. The printed forms note the transfer of the bodies to the cemetery. Several other notices, such as that of a baptism, are also included. While the documents span nearly half of the 19th century, the preponderance date from the 1860s and 1870s. An interesting collection that sheds light on the Cuban bureaucracy surrounding slavery, which continued on the island until 1888. Smathers Libraries, University of Florida		0	2017	0039			2017-05-09 00:00:00.000	Manuscripts - Florida History Collections	The Pattillo Family Collection contains photographs, diplomas, certificates, and histories of the Pattillo family in Volusia County, Florida.  Most of the material relates to Alfred Thomas Pattillo’s children, particularly Lovick, Anne, Nell, and Lewis.  There are photos of students at Florida Agricultural College in Lake City and Florida State College in Tallahassee from the time when Lovick, Millard, Anne, and Nell attended in the early 1900s.  Other photographs depict residents of Osteen, Florida, in the 1880s and 1890s; flooding in New Smyrna in 1924 (almost 24 inches of rain fell in 24 hours); and members of the Pattillo family.  The collection also contains five scrapbooks of photos, primarily collected by Anne, Nell, and Lewis.  Most of the photos are of family members, but the albums also include tourist photos of areas around Florida in the first decades of the twentieth century, including New Smyrna, Coronado Beach, and St. Augustine.  One of the albums also includes photos of students from Stetson University, probably from the time that Anne and Nell were in college.  The diplomas and certificates in the collection are from the Florida Agricultural College Military Department, the University of Florida, the Masons, and the Shriners. In addition, the collection contains family histories told in reminiscences of James L. Pattillo and Era Woodward Pattillo.  Similar documents on the school and store in Osteen, Florida, were written either by Anne or Nell Pattillo.   | 	Pictures; flood- 8, Deland- 21, Florida-25, family and community-25, Photo albums; #1-214, #2-76, #3-53, #4-64, #5-76, New Smyrna-8, F.A.C.-34, F.S.C.-5 pictures. W.	0	2017	0044			2015-07-18 00:00:00.000	Manuscripts - Judaica Collections	A Yemenite liturgical MS codex (incomplete) containing lamentations (qinot), penitential hymns (selichot and maranot) for the Ninth of Av and for mourners in Hebrew and Aramaic. Includes compositions of the medieval Hebrew poets of Spain (Solomon Ibn Gabirol, Judah ha-Levi, Abraham Ibn Ezra) and other well-known hymns of the Sephardi rite, as well as poems known only from the Yemenite rite. Also, bound into the codex are astronomical texts in Judaeo-Arabic, including mention of lunar mansions and prognostications by quivering. Other leaves are hidden between the leather, but they are too damaged and crumbled to retrieve. The version of the prayer for the dead (Kaddish) is according to the Baladi (local) Yemenite rite. |  | Manuscript codex (incomplete); 23 x 16 cm; 111ff: 110 ff. of handmade paper with horizontal chain lines and "tre lune" watermarks of the Venetian Valentino Galvani paper mill, and one folio of modern commercial paper (f.98). Staining and water damage to many leaves; some loose leaves; leather and cloth sack binding. The texts are handwritten in balck ink by multiple scribes; some leaves show evidence of scribal practice. The liturgical texts are vocalized with Babylonian supra-linear vowel signs. One leaf of parchment and several crumbling leaves are hidden in the binding. 1836	4	2017-10-30 10:54:27.863	2017-08-15 11:53:09.093	mjkruse	mjkruse	José Moskovits Anti-Semitism Collection		1976	2017	1976	1979	1.16	35 folders in 2 boxes	Linear feet	Moskovits, Jose´	Special and Area Studies Collections, George A. Smathers Libraries, University of Florida		0	2017	0048			2017-04-01 00:00:00.000	Manuscripts - Judaica Collections	Collection of correspondences on antisemitism. Letters, short essays, art, newspaper clippings. |  | An extraordinary world-wide study on anti-Semitism. José Moskovits (1926-2014), a Holocaust survivor and prominent Argentinean reparations lawyer, is also known for his role in helping with the capture of Eichmann and the search for Mengele. In the 1970s, at the height of Argentina’s Dirty War and following on from the UN declaration that Zionism is Racism, Moskovits decided to create an incredible survey of seven questions on the eternal problem and nature of anti-Semitism. He compiled a list of 5,000 world leaders in politics, business and religion, as well as from the arts and sciences, and sent them the survey. He received around 1,000 responses (including world leaders like Margaret Thatcher, Willy Brandt, and the King of Morocco) in which many of the writers share their thoughts on anti-Semitism, and many supply additional comments on discrimination and human rights in general. This collection will inspire many research projects, particularly within the fields of human rights, international studies, political science, sociology, psychology, Latin American studies and Jewish studies. Smathers Libraries, University of Florida	Asher Rare Books & Antiquariaat FORUM.	0	2017	0049			2017-07-28 00:00:00.000	Manuscripts - Latin American and Caribbean Collections	Official transcript made in 1831 of a testament drawn up at St. Jago de la Vega, Jamaica |  |  primary source for slavery in Jamaica, five years before its legal abolition in 1834. Although the British parliament legally abolished the African slave trade in their territories in 1808, they did not legally abolish the ownership of slaves until 1834. The present last will and testament of the merchant Joseph Barnes (ca. 1765?-6 May 1829) of Kingston, Jamaica, made at nearby St. Jago de la Vega (now Spanish Town), then the capital of Jamaica, records his ownership of estates in St Catharine parish (surrounding St. Jago de la Vega). He traded extensively in cotton and was mayor of Kingston from 1823 to 1829.He left the largest estates with their slaves in the care of his brother Thomas: the Cumberland Pen estate of more than a thousand acres along with "all and every negro and other slaves thereunto belonging ." and another smaller one, together nearly 500 slaves. He made provisions for the care of his wife Hannah and their daughter Charlotte Hannah Barnes (ca. 1800-1876) based on the income from these estates. The present official copy was made when the will was proved by a firm of "proctors" in Doctor's Commons, a society of lawyers in London.A small piece of the seal has broken off but still present, and the document shows slight wear at the folds and some dirt and spots, but is otherwise in very good condition. Bookseller Inventory #  |  | Administration (with the will annexed) of Joseph Barnes esqr. deceased[,] dated 9th November 1831[.] Extracted by Farquhar Sladen & Glennie - Proctors[,] Doctors Commons.[London], 9 November 1831. 134 x 79 cm (folded to 17 x 27 cm). Official transcript made in 1831 of a testament drawn up on 4 February 1822 and proved there on 30 May 1829, written in a very large upright engrossing hand. With the Doctor's Commons' probate form (20 x 20 cm) attached with the large embossed seal of the prerogative court of the Archbishop of Canterbury. Most in Spanish (untranslated), some in English; most from Havana, some from Paris, London and Spain. Feb. 1855-Nov. 1856. Approximately 36 total pages + stampless address leaves. |   | Born in Spain, Ceballos immigrated to colonial Cuba, then moved to New York, where he laid the foundation for his son to become the “J.P.Morgan of Cuba” after the Spanish-American War, with vast financial interests in Cuban construction, shipping and sugar (and even in the breweries of New York), |   | After his father’s death in 1886, the younger Ceballos became a power on Wall Street, hobnobbing with Harriman and Huntington until his company failed in 1906, when its Havana representative absconded with millions of dollars. |  | These letters, written 50 years earlier, detail the birth of the Ceballos firm, when its ties to Spanish Cuba included a Havana company linked to the slave trade (and, possibly, to Confederate gun runners during the American Civil War.) Though the elder Ceballos may have moved to the US earlier, he first appeared in New York newspapers in October 1855, as co-owner of the “New York and Mexican Steamship Line” that sailed to Havana, Vera Cruz and Cadiz. So these business letters may reveal much about the birth of Cuban-American finance. | 		Very good	Purchase	NULL	NULL	NULL		NULL			0	0				Purchased from The Philadelphia Rare Books & Manuscript Company in 2017. Smathers Libraries, University of Florida		0	2017	0059			2017-05-31 00:00:00.000	Manuscripts - Florida History Collections	Manuscript, sketches, and clippings documenting Ivar Widing’s two-thousand-mile journey from Boston to Key West during the winter of 1915-1916. |  | The Ivar Widing Collection contains materials related to Widing’s two-thousand-mile journey from Boston to Key West during the winter of 1915-1916.  The collection includes two copies of Widing’s manuscript, “A Two-Thousand Mile Midwinter Cruise in a 12-foot Boat;” pencil and ink sketches illustrating the manuscript; clippings about Widing and his journey; promotional materials for lectures given by Widing; company stationery for Widing’s businesses, which includes an image of the “Wanderer”; a small selection of sketches not related to his excursion; and an unidentified list of addresses.		Conservation Note |  | Sketches were inspected by John Freund on May 24, 2017 and should be protected due to their brittle nature. The other materials should be inspected and flattened/repaired if needed. Plan is to store items together in a flat or clam-shell box. |  | Submitted by James Cusick, May 31, 2017.
